<Date>1498279755597<//Date><Rating>3</Rating>< Text>
I love shopping at the large health food grocery stores they are so much fun to wonder around in and just  look at all the interesting vitamins and groceries and orchard is no different ,but unfortunately looking is all the average person can do, because healthy and unprocessed is expensive  and orchards seem to be even a little more expensive then their contemporaries. With that being said  I am not sure orchards prices can be justified, but in all fairness I feel that most of the health food industry would be hard pressed to justify their gauging anyway. In a world where so many are either going hungry or being poisoned by genetically modified foods there entipeniral practices appears to be like black mail. I wreary of  hearing this industry criticize the medical world and their prices, and in the next breath ask some single mothers who dared to pause at the price of there better then ever 8 oz bottle of the newest healing elixir what she would pay for her health and that of her families.
The prices that the health food and the organic vitimine industry charges are unobtainable for the average budget.  SO I give them and all the health food industry a three star for being facinating and interesting but no higher  because I feel the entire industry denies  the ecconomically challenge fair  access to good nutrition and health and in so doing they show a lacks of humanity and integrity. They judge the medical world for the outrageous prices on medicine and services and yet they charge price that are just as outrageous with out the relief of medical insurence so for the most part I will just stick to Wal-Mart At least Sam Waltons legacy is preferable to living under a bridge while slurping up a containers of 16 oz 7.00 yogurt. NO THANK YOU!</Text>

This woman thought me and my parents were going to steal from Goodwill. It is a decent size store. Seems to be well organized, I went early on a Thursday morning. The shoe racks are in order by color. They have a variety selection of shoes for women. The shoe rack for men is a very small selection and seems to have a lot of big sized shoes. The furniture selection was pretty good from what I saw. For the childrens department, there were about 4 racks of clothes, most for other kids sizes 5/6 and up. Parking for this location is limited so good luck on a busy morning like Thursdays. Over all I would say some of the stuff I found were over priced to be second hand. I walked out empty handed, didn't find much of a bargain.<//Text>

< text>
Honestly one of the best thrift shops that I have been to in my entire life, and I am someone who loves Goodwill wherever I am in this country. The supply for this store is so great they fill many dumpsters a day with stuff they couldn't take, and they have new stuff coming out on the floor on roller carts roughly every 20 minutes. I think part of what makes the selection so good here is the proximity to very expensive parts of E. Pasadena, although I usually see hoodlums like myself shopping there. The‚Äã record selection is pretty insane here; I have yet to get a portable turntable but have seriously considered it for this store alone. There is always a tag of the day which costs one dollar, so tons of people come in as regular and just hunt the dollar deals as a stress reliever/cheap shopping activity. The plastic bags they use are huge, and I'm not kidding when I say they work both as a kitchen trash bag and as a rain poncho. If you like to shop vintage and live in or around Pasadena (it is on Metro Bus line 181), definitely check this Goodwill out and you won't regret it. Plus, you're helping employ a bunch of people who really need it. Win-win!</text>

< time>
1557245446718< /time>
<rate>5< /rate>< Text>
Visited on May 5, 2019.

From the look outside, it doesn't seem too appealing, but when you get inside, it's quite a cozy little restaurant. The restaurant had a very homely type of atmosphere and there are probably enough to fit 30-40 people in.

Aside from the atmosphere, Mama's Asian Noodle House has a bunch of Thai/Lao food which will make your mouth water. As a family of 6, we ordered about 3 orders of the pork belly, and to be quite honest, I think we should've ordered atleast 4! The pork belly was so tender, so crispy, and so delicious that it was almost addicting.

My dad ordered some type of pho and that too tasted marvelous. I don't know the exact name of the pho, but I am assuming most their phos will taste just as good. The rest of the family ordered the fried rice (beef & shrimp ($2.00+ extra)) and I think it's better to order the shrimp. Both tasted fantastic and can rival fried rice from other places. Last, my family ordered the papaya salad (watch out, it's spicy), and they said even though it was spicy, it was really good.

We rate the restaurant as 5/5, taking inputs from my family. This place is a great place to visit!< /Text>

Great restaurant! I've been here several times. The style of food is very unique, not just your typical Vietnamese pho place. It seems like the chef was maybe trained in culinary school, as the menu covers a lot of ground. But everything I've tried here, from the pho, to the curry, to the typical spicy chicken entree, all of it is very tasty, as well as VERY aesthetically attractive.
The women waiting on you are very friendly and attentive, prices are very fair... what else can you ask for? You definitely need to try this place when in the mood for some Asian food that's a little outside the box.< /text>

<text>Service was extremely friendly and attentive. I was very happy with how quick our orders were taken and waters refilled.

We got the Thai boat noodle, crispy pork belly, and pad see ew.

The good:

Crispy pork belly was indeed crispy and overall good. But if you've ever been to LA and had some from Sam woo, you'll know that the pork is not as tender as it could be. The skin was slightly stale (too much chew, it should break apart a little easier). Even so, it is not a bad dish. B-

The pad see ew was flavorful with a good amount of meat and veggies. Noodles were more on the Al dente side which is something I prefer even though pad see ew usually has softer noodles. Nothing phenomenal, still good execution, B+.

Bathroom and interior is well lit and clean.

The bad:

The Thai boat noodle was so damn salty. It had way too much of the soup base. I like my noodle soup with the ingredients kind of unseasoned, it balances a flavorful broth. That is not the case here.

We went so far as to remove the noodles and meat out of the soup. And you could still taste the broth (and salt!) in the ingredients.

I think they overshot the time the rice noodles need in boiling water and, personally, I don't think the water needs to be salted. Maybe a little would be okay, but the Thai boat base was already too much to handle.

Thai boat noodle gets a D.

Parking is easy, area isn't super nice, but that can't really be helped. I'd come again, but I wouldn't make a grand effort. Overall, it was okay, C+.<//text></record></dataset><record>

< review>
Uhoh. When you see a lot of writing, it's going to be a complaint!

Let me start with saying that the workers are all at least friendly and nice. The store is clean and in a nice location. The pizza tastes like it should with evenly-dispersed toppings and properly-baked crust and whatnot.

Here's the problem: Don't order from this Dominos if you want your pizza properly sliced. Most people don't care, I'm sure, if one slice is a little off. I don't. When it's bisected into a third and two thirds, it's a problem. When ten or more pizzas are ordered and they're all that way, it's a problem. When the same or similar order comes in every week at the same time from the same place and the pizzas are all still cut badly, it's a problem. One would think that some care would be put into making pizzas for repeat customers who spend over $100 per week on pizza orders. (Before you start thinking I'm a fatty - which I am - I'm not just ordering for myself.) I asked once for them to cut my pizzas evenly and nothing changed. This tells me that the Dominos workers don't care about the one product they're actually known for.

Thank you for for the good times, Dominos, but "You have failed me for the last time."

My name is Martin Reid, and this is my story.<//review>

< Text>
Visited here on January 19th 2021.  The experience was exceptional from beginning to end.  I didn't get a chance to catch the names of the people who worked with me because we arrived just in time for the cut-off time off 1:45pm for boat rentals and we were  rushing through until we could settle in on the lake.  Now I know where to go on weekends if I have a window of 3 hours.  It's nearby, yet worlds away.  Highly recommend.  Just please keep it as beautiful, clean, peaceful as it is.< /Text>

<Text>Gorgeous place, and very environmentally conscious as well!

Excellent for paddle boarding, boating, lounging by the beach, fishing, horse back riding, etc. If you do bring a boat or board or similar gear, you will have to have them inspected when entering the area to avoid contaminating the lake with invasive species. That means your gear MUST BE DRY or that equipment will have a one week ban from the park.

Highly recommend!</Text>< pics>

After going thru a overwhelmingly negative set of reviews I still chose to go to this store to repair my phone hoping my experience would be different. My phone‚Äôs limited warranty was also quickly coming to an end and hence I thought replacing the battery within the period would waive the charges for it which was also reaffirmed to me multiple times calling apple support and also their technicians. Some of my observations of this store based on my experience:

Most of the associates in the support team are very young and inexperienced - the first time I was late to my appointment and I was given a second chance to see the next available support technician within 15 minutes and I ended up spending half an hour and when I spoke to that person who assured me someone will see me in fifteen minutes, went thru the log and then stated that it will be longer since they were so backed up. Not sure why he couldn‚Äôt have told me this prior to me having to wait half hour there with no assurance anyone will show up.

The second time, a technician did see me and she told me that I will need to bring my phone and hand it over to them for the repair the next day since they were not taking in anymore work orders for the day. I was alright with that. I told her that I was on the last day of my warranty and that they should replace the battery with no cost to me as I was assured by apple support over the phone. She also confirmed that to be true and she showed me a page where the cost was indicated as zero dollars and asked for me to sign after reading the terms. Little did I know that she had also conflictingly stated that the battery replacement was to be charged since although I was under warranty, the battery report came out to be good and I insisted on replacing it anyway. The reason why I wanted the battery replaced was because it was draining very quickly even without me actively using the phone and I noticed this behavior after the latest OS upgrades.

The next day I went to give my phone for repair and the person that collected it also reconfirmed that I shall not be charged. All the whole they were entering a truly conflicting statement in their reports. When I went to collect the phone in the evening, the person that showed up with the phone insisted I pay for the battery and I refused stating that I have been told this is covered under warranty. Then the manager shows up with all the logs from the previous support folks clearly stating that the battery was to be charged while verbally they were telling me otherwise and getting me to sign the understanding that we had. The manager started making statements that this was a he said-she said thing and that the paperwork was clearly reflective of the cost associated with the new battery and legally am supposed to pay the fee.

I had been lied to multiple times in the store with multiple support staff claiming I don‚Äôt owe anything for the new battery while they have been entering a completely different thing in their notes. I paid for the battery and told the manager I will never come back to this store again. Even if I am crazy enough to buy another apple product it shall be online and for support I‚Äôd much rather go to the SF support centers.

Please avoid this store at all costs - or else read the fine print before you sign. These support staff are either too young and naive or grossly misleading not even knowing what assurances they are giving their customers.</Review>

<Text>Multiple bad experiences with this store. Being an embedded software engineer myself, I can tell they BS a lot, at times dispensing false or useless information or advice. Imagine what it would be like for those who are not in the technology field.

I felt that the interaction with people there, if it did not lead to a purchase or repair, there would be no record. If you want to complain, there's no case number to refer to. You would just have to make general remark. Can't go back to the specific person I talked to. Hence, in many cases, there's no accountability. They just say whatever.

I replaced the iPhone 6 battery. It started to act up around 2 year. It may be true that the battery had reached end of life, and OS update did not play essential role, it's still a cost that people need to consider when purchasing a phone. Why not put a bigger battery for such premium phone? I think it's pretty universal at this point that, we don't need the phone to be any more thinner, and people want more battery, hence not only we have more battery life for daily use, the battery would also last longer.

When I signed off for the battery replacement, I did not know before hand that they said in the paper work that my phone has cosmetic damage. If I knew, I would certainly contest and ask for explaintion. This is they covering their rear end. I don't appreciate at all.

After I left my phone for battery replacement, I was told it would take 2 hours and they will email me, since they can't call me. I waited 2 and a half hours, and went back and checked, it was already done, but no email. I think for iPhone 6, it should be done for less than 30 minutes. I should have checked back earlier.

My iPhone 6 at one point showing battery stuck at 100%. I didn't know how much battery actually left and the phone could shut down any time. But when I described it people standing at the front, I was told, something to the effect that, "It's good, you never run out of battery".

One of the "Genius" there lacked the understanding of the "advices" she's giving out and didn't know what customer service is. She said my phone is low on storage that we could not do firmware upgrade. I said that's not true. The OS had been upgraded with the capability to uninstall apps in the background to free up space. I showed her that my iPad did just that.

She said a phone needed 20% or some crazy percentage of free space to operate properly. I asked her, if that's true for phones with 32GB storage and 128GB storage. It obviously doesn't make sense.

She asked me if I know what MB is. And she said the OS does not show the accurate free space left, and since I don't believe her, she asked me to add up the storage space used by all apps. Again, she asked a customer to add up the storage space used by all the apps! Is this what Apple is?

I asked if she could run some diagnostics, she declined, saying she could not.

At this point, she said she could not help me, and started the preparation for the next customer.

When I picked up my phone after the battery replacement, the same "genius" happened to be the person handing me the phone. Not sure she's not doing the genius work any more, or part of their responsibilities. Not sure if she remembered me, but she's giving out more false information, claiming the battery has 7000 charge cycles. I was just like, whatever. I thanked her, grabbed my phone and left for good.< /Text>< pictures>

<text>The Apple Store is the only place I've been that's managed to make buying electronics feel awkward.

I went there once because I had a gift card and wanted to buy an external hard drive for my MacBook. I knew which one I wanted, so I walked to the back of the store and picked it up. Easy.

But then it came time to pay for the thing. Most stores have a checkout area at the front where they scan your stuff and tell you the total, but not Apple Stores. At an Apple Store, you've gotta find an employee who isn't busy and get them to scan it with their iPhone.

There's no good strategy for doing this; all the employees are either already helping customers or taking to their co-workers, so you can either interrupt someone or stand around awkwardly until one of them walks up to you. For a company that prides itself on being cool, it just feels... weird.

Sure, I've had alright experiences picking up online orders and getting support, but actually buying anything is painful enough that I'd recommend going online or to a carrier store instead.<//text><Pics>None< /Pics><Response>None<//Response>< Gmap_id>

<rating>1</rating><Text>Dear Apple,

I tried replacing my battery for $29 today‚Ä¶ I wasn‚Äôt able to, not today, tomorrow, or next week. I first spent 39 minutes on the phone with your help line this morning (32 of which were on hold), and unfortunately we were not able to find an open appointment at my local Apple store (or any within 50 miles of me) this MONTH. I was instructed to check if there is a walk in appointment available. I made my way down to the Stoneridge Shopping Center and immediately realized my chances were slim to none. Nevertheless, I waited in the line to speak with an employee. I found out my options were as follows:

-Wait for 5-7 hours today to possibly qualify for a walk in appointment
-Come in earlier tomorrow to have a better shot of qualifying for that appointment
-Wait 2 weeks to schedule an appointment during work hours
-And of course, I also have the option of sending my phone in to Apple to be fixed, which costs closer to $40 with shipping and takes ‚Äúabout 5 business days‚Äù

According to my calculations, either way I break it down I pay more than $70 for this battery. Including this trip to the mall I would have to make at least 2 more, the mall is 20 minutes away from my house and costs at least $5 in gas roundtrip, that‚Äôs already another $15 assuming my time is free. Being that my time isn‚Äôt free, especially on Mondays when I‚Äôm at work, I figure I lose another $40+.

A piece of information I found to be truly amazing is that if by some miracle my phone found its way into the hands of an Apple employee, then first a test has to be conducted which should take 15-20 minutes, then only if there is a battery in stock I will be granted the privilege to wait for 2-3 hours for an Apple specialist to replace my battery. Once again‚Ä¶ only if there is a battery in stock.

Fortunately, this story had a happy ending. I walked down to the phone repair booth in the mall and the 2 employees there that deal with 60+ phones daily were able to replace my battery in under 15 minutes for $45.

I would imagine that if Apple really had its customers‚Äô best interests in mind it would invest either in training for its sales people to replace the battery (a very easy task according to Youtube) or would deploy more ‚ÄúApple Specialists‚Äù to various stores.
